GT Equivalence Verification (BPG5)

GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4/(c5*P + c6)
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to find the GT expression and see if any candidate can match it.

**GT expression:**
$$f(P) = 0.9198(1 - P/84.03)P + 0.9198 \cdot P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

Let me expand this:
$$f(P) = 0.9198P - 0.9198P^2/84.03 + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$
$$= 0.9198P - 0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

This is a function of P only (no t dependence). So I need candidates that can reduce to a function of P only.

The key structural challenge is the term $P^2/(aP + 1)$, which is a rational function. Let me rewrite it:
$$P^2/(7.531P + 1) = P/7.531 - P/(7.531(7.531P + 1)) \cdot 1/7.531$$

Actually, let me check: $P^2/(aP+1) = P/a - (P/a)/(aP+1) = P/a - 1/a^2 + 1/(a^2(aP+1))$

So $P^2/(aP+1) = P/a - 1/a^2 + 1/(a^2(aP+1))$

The GT becomes: $\alpha P - \beta P^2 + \gamma[P/a - 1/a^2 + 1/(a^2(aP+1))]$

This has terms: $P^2$, $P$, constant, and $1/(aP+1)$.

**Candidate 47:** $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2/(P+c_3) + c_4$

Note that $Pc_2/(P+c_3)$ can be rewritten. Let me check if GT can be expressed this way.

GT = $-0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$

Rewriting $0.9198P^2/(7.531P+1)$: factor out from numerator:
$$0.9198P^2/(7.531P+1) = 0.1222P \cdot P/(P + 1/7.531) = 0.1222P \cdot P/(P + 0.1328)$$

So $0.9198P^2/(7.531P+1) = 0.1222 \cdot P^2/(P + 0.1328)$

Now decompose: $P^2/(P+c) = P - c + c^2/(P+c)$

So $0.1222[P - 0.1328 + 0.01763/(P+0.1328)]$

GT = $-0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P + 0.1222P - 0.01623 + 0.002154/(P+0.1328)$
GT = $-0.01095P^2 + 1.042P - 0.01623 + 0.002154/(P+0.1328)$

**Candidate 46:** $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + c_2 t \exp(c_3 t) + c_4 + c_5/(P+c_6)$

Setting $c_2 = 0$ eliminates the t-dependent term. Then: $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + c_4 + c_5/(P+c_6)$

This gives: $P^2$, $P$, constant, $1/(P+c_6)$ — exactly the form we need!

Set: $c_0 = -0.01095$, $c_1 = 1.042$, $c_2 = 0$, $c_4 = -0.01623$, $c_5 = 0.002154$, $c_6 = 0.1328$.

This matches the GT perfectly!

Let me verify candidate 47 also works: $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2/(P+c_3) + c_4$

$Pc_2/(P+c_3)$: We need $1/(P+c_6)$ not $P/(P+c)$. But $P/(P+c) = 1 - c/(P+c)$, so $Pc_2/(P+c_3) = c_2 - c_2 c_3/(P+c_3)$. This gives constant + $1/(P+c_3)$ term. So candidate 47 also works: $P^2(-0.01095) + P(1.042) + P \cdot c_2/(P+0.1328) + c_4$. We need $c_2 \cdot P/(P+0.1328)$ to produce $-0.01623 + 0.002154/(P+0.1328)$, so $c_2 - c_2(0.1328)/(P+0.1328)$, meaning $c_2(0.1328) = -0.002154$, giving $c_2 = -0.01622$. Then constant from this: $c_2 = -0.01622$, plus $c_4$, total constant = $c_4 - 0.01622 = -0.01623$, so $c_4 ≈ 0$. Works!

[MATCH FOUND]

Candidates **46** and **47** can both match the GT with appropriate constant choices. Candidate 46 with $c_2=0$ gives $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + c_4 + c_5/(P+c_6)$, matching the expanded GT form exactly.

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

**GT expression:**
$$f(P) = 0.9198(1 - P/84.03)P + 0.9198 \cdot P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

Let me expand this:
$$f(P) = 0.9198P - 0.9198P^2/84.03 + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$
$$= 0.9198P - 0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

The key structural feature is: **a polynomial in P (linear + quadratic terms) plus a rational function** $P^2/(aP + 1)$. Note that the GT depends only on P, not on t.

The rational term $\frac{P^2}{7.531P + 1}$ cannot be simplified to a polynomial. Let me check what forms can match.

**Key observation:** $\frac{P^2}{aP+1}$ can be rewritten. Long division: $P^2/(aP+1) = P/a - 1/a^2 + 1/(a^2(aP+1))$. So GT = quadratic polynomial in P + $c/(aP+1)$ term.

Equivalently: GT = $\alpha P^2 + \beta P + \gamma + \delta/(aP+1)$ for some constants.

Let me verify: $0.9198P^2/(7.531P+1) = 0.9198[P/7.531 - 1/7.531^2 + 1/(7.531^2(7.531P+1))]$
$= 0.1221P - 0.01621 + 0.01621/(7.531P+1) \cdot 7.531... $

Actually let me just keep it as: GT has the form $aP^2 + bP + c + d/(eP+1)$ where $c$ and $d$ come from the rational part decomposition.

Now let me check each candidate for structural compatibility:

**Candidates that are pure polynomials in P (no rational/transcendental terms involving P):**
- Candidates 1, 6, 8, 11, 14, 16: These are polynomials in P only. A polynomial CANNOT equal a function with a $1/(aP+1)$ term. **NO MATCH** for all of these.

**Candidates with t-dependence that cannot be zeroed:**
- Candidate 2: has $c2\cdot\log(1+c3/P)$ - this is a log term in P, not equivalent to $1/(eP+1)$. Also $c4/t^5$ can be zeroed. But log term doesn't match. **NO MATCH**
- Candidate 3: $c3\cdot t\cdot\exp(c4\cdot t)$ can be zeroed (c3=0). Then: $aP^2 + bP + c5 + c6/(c7 P^2+1)$. The rational term is $1/(P^2+c)$ not $1/(P+c)$. **NO MATCH**
- Candidate 4: Zero t-term (c2=0). Then $aP^2+bP+c4+c5\log(c6 P+1)$. Log ≠ rational. **NO MATCH**
- Candidate 5: Zero t-terms. $aP^2+bP+c5+c6\exp(c7 P^2)$. Exp ≠ rational. **NO MATCH**

- Candidate 13: Same. **NO MATCH**
- Candidate 15: Has Max(0, P+c6). Piecewise linear ≠ rational. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 47:** $P^2 c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(P+c3) + c4$

This is: $c0 P^2 + c1 P + c2 P/(P+c3) + c4$

Now $c2 P/(P+c3) = c2[1 - c3/(P+c3)] = c2 - c2 c3/(P+c3)$

So this equals: $c0 P^2 + c1 P + c2 + c4 - c2 c3/(P+c3)$

GT = $\alpha P^2 + \beta P + \gamma + \delta/(eP+1)$. This matches the form! With $c3 = 1/e$, etc. **MATCH**
